- Sprint 10.5 Phase 2 (this PR) — **MCQ format for personalized D1 + session/attempt wire (Andy decision after Phase 1 quality inspection).** Phase 1 (PR #204 + #205) shipped free-text infra. Andy's manual inspection of 10 random Phase 1 generations revealed two systemic issues: (a) AI sometimes generated ungrammatical sentences forcing the target form (e.g. "she felt completely rejuvenate" instead of "rejuvenated"), and (b) `acceptable_variants` coverage was incomplete for verb inflections. Andy locked Option A (MCQ format) — sidesteps the grammar issue (user selects from buttons, doesn't type), sidesteps the variant coverage gap (validation is exact-option match), and matches the actual current `d1-exercise.js` UX (which was MCQ all along — Phase 1 spec's "match current UX" claim was a misread that Code flagged during implementation). Trade-off: lose productive-recall benefit; deferred to a future "recall mode" toggle once prompt quality matures. **Schema (migrations 053 + 054).** Migration 053 adds `options JSONB NOT NULL DEFAULT '[]'::jsonb` to `user_d1_questions` — array of 4 option strings, pre-shuffled at generation time. Migration 054 drops the FK constraint on `vocabulary_exercise_attempts.exercise_id` (added by migration 022 to reference admin pool only) and adds `exercise_source TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT 'admin'` with a CHECK constraint (`'admin' | 'personalized'`). Polymorphic discriminator lets a single attempts table log against either source. The 'admin' default backfills the existing rows without a separate sweep. Both migrations idempotent. **AI generator (`services/d1_question_generator.py`).** System prompt rewritten with explicit STEP 1 (sentence) + STEP 2 (3 distractors) instructions. JSON schema now includes a `distractors` array of length 3 alongside `context_sentence`, `target_answer`, `acceptable_variants`, `hint`. Validation gained `_normalize_distractors` (reject if not exactly 3 entries / target appears in distractors / case-insensitive duplicates) and `_shuffled_options(target, distractors, seed=headword)` that builds a 4-element MCQ array using `random.Random(seed).shuffle()` for deterministic order across runs. Evidence-substring fallback intentionally returns `options=[]` (no AI = no distractors) and is documented to be filled by the Phase 2 backfill in a separate pass. **Phase 2 backfill (`scripts/backfill_d1_questions_mcq.py`, NEW).** Walks rows with `options=[]` (Phase 1 leftovers + evidence-fallback inserts), calls a cheaper distractor-only Haiku prompt, UPDATEs `options` with the shuffled 4-element array. Idempotent — rows with `len(options) == 4` are skipped. 100ms rate limit between calls. **Session endpoint refactor (`routers/exercises.py` `start_d1_session`).** New flow: (1) query `user_d1_questions` for active rows where `len(options) == 4` (MCQ-ready only — rows with empty options are skipped, the session never renders a broken card); (2) prefer unattempted personalized first, attempted as review fill; (3) take up to `size` rows; (4) if personalized count < size, top up from admin pool via the existing `_pull_admin` helper. Each session row carries a `source` tag (`personalized` | `admin_fallback`) and a `target_vocabulary_id` (Sprint 10.3 SRS wire requirement). Sprint 10.5 Phase 2 deferred items: 70/30 due/new ratio per SRS state (would need a JOIN with `flashcard_reviews` — Phase 2 prefers ALL personalized regardless of SRS due date; adds value without immediate user-visible regression). New helper `_personalized_session_view(row)` builds the same shape as `_session_exercise_view` so the frontend has one rendering path; `context_sentence` is rendered with the target word replaced by `___` (existing UI's blank marker) using the stored `blank_position_start/_end` (defensive substring-replace fallback if positions are malformed). **Attempt handler refactor (`submit_d1_attempt`).** Polymorphic dispatch: try `user_d1_questions` first via the user-scoped Supabase client (RLS scopes to caller), then fall back to the admin pool (`vocabulary_exercises`) on miss. `correct_answer` and `target_vocab_id` plumb through to Sprint 10.3's `_apply_d1_srs_update` from either source. Attempt INSERT now carries `exercise_source` ('personalized' or 'admin') so analytics + per-source rate-limit tuning are possible later. Sprint 10.3 first-attempt detection + Sprint 10.4 pending-vocab guard preserved unchanged. **Frontend (`frontend/js/d1-exercise.js` + `pages/d1-exercise.html`).** Source label primitive `.d1-source-label` with `--personalized` (teal pill, "Từ vốn từ của bạn") and `--admin` (muted grey pill, "Bài luyện tập chung") variants. Conditional emission via `ex.source === 'personalized' ? ... : ex.source === 'admin_fallback' ? ... : ''` — legacy payloads without `source` render no label (graceful fallback). Inline `<style>` block in d1-exercise.html gained the two variant rules. Existing MCQ rendering (option buttons, local-grade, Sprint 10.3 SRS indicator) untouched. **Tests (+15 net new):** Backend: `test_d1_question_generator.py` gained 6 new MCQ contracts (Haiku payload includes distractors; distractors missing/wrong-count/equal-to-target/duplicate all reject the AI payload; evidence fallback returns `options=[]`; deterministic shuffle reproducibility) + 3 existing tests updated to pass the new distractors-required validation. `test_backfill_d1_questions_mcq.py` (NEW, 3 tests) — augments rows with empty options, idempotent on second run, continues after distractor-generation returns None. `test_d1_session.py` gained 7 new tests — session prefers personalized, admin fallback when personalized short, skips rows with `len(options) != 4`, blank-marker rendering, attempt grading routes to personalized table, wrong answer fires `rating='again'`. Frontend: `tests/d1-source-label.test.mjs` (NEW, 6 sentinels) — Vietnamese labels present, exact source string matches, both BEM variant classes emitted, both inline styles declared, legacy-payload graceful empty-string fallback. **Backend pytest: 1010 passed / 23 skipped / 0 failed** (+15 net new vs Phase 1-hotfix baseline 995). **Frontend node tests: 2648 passed / 0 failed** (+6 net new vs Sprint 10.4.1-hotfix baseline 2642). **Spec falsifications (cumulative 41-43):** (41) `target_answer` still sent in session response for local-grade consistency with admin pool — spec asked for server-grade only on personalized but switching mid-flight breaks the existing PHASE_D §5 contract ("D1 không phải exam — local grade an toàn"). Deferred to 10.5.x when admin pool sunset begins. (42) 70/30 due/new split deferred — adds value without immediate user-visible regression and requires a JOIN with `flashcard_reviews` that complicates the session query. Sprint 10.5.x candidate. (43) `vocabulary_exercise_attempts.exercise_id` FK dropped in migration 054 — referential integrity now enforced at the application layer (attempt handler validates the id resolves to one of the two source tables before INSERT). Pragmatic call: alternative is splitting attempts across two tables, which doubles the rate-limit query cost. **Audit hotfix count: unchanged at 24** — Sprint 10.5 Phase 2 is foundation 5/9 of the Sprint 10.0 Option A roadmap, not a hotfix. Foundation 5/9 (Personalized D1) now COMPLETE. Refs Sprint 10.0 discovery Issue #8, Area 2, DEBT-VOCAB-WORKFLOW. Andy's Phase 2 quality-inspection signal (10 random Phase 1 samples → MCQ decision) memorialized as a process win — Phase split + quality gate before user-facing surface flip prevented shipping the free-text bugs.
- Sprint 10.5 Phase 1-hotfix — **Fix `part_of_speech` → `pos` column-name mismatch.** Sprint 10.5 Phase 1 (PR #204) code referenced `user_vocabulary.part_of_speech` in three places (backfill script SELECT, confirm-hook helper SELECT in `vocabulary_bank.py`, generator dict access in `d1_question_generator.py`), but Sprint 10.1 migration 049 added the column as `pos` (short name, spaCy convention). Andy's first backfill run errored on `column user_vocabulary.part_of_speech does not exist` (Postgres 42703). The `BackgroundTask` from `/pending/confirm` hit the same failure but was silenced by the fail-soft `try/except` (logged at WARN, returned `None`). **Fix (Pattern A — replace, not alias):** `part_of_speech` → `pos` across all three Sprint 10.5 user_vocabulary sites + two test fixtures. Separate `content_vocab` MD frontmatter subsystem (`services/vocab_content.py`, `backend/content_vocab/**/*.md`, `frontend/js/vocabulary.js`, `test_vocab_content.py`) keeps `part_of_speech` as the canonical YAML key — that's a different schema with its own consumers, untouched. **Regression test added** (`test_backfill_d1_questions.py::test_backfill_select_uses_canonical_pos_column_name`): asserts the three Sprint 10.5 source files contain zero `part_of_speech` references AND contain `pos`, so a future PR re-introducing the long name trips here. Source-file string snapshot rather than a live DB connection so the test runs without Supabase. **Backend pytest: 995 passed / 23 skipped / 0 failed** (+1 net new regression test vs Phase 1 baseline 994). **Spec falsification (40):** column-naming drift between sprints. Sprint 10.1 chose `pos` (short, schema-side); Sprint 10.5 spec used `part_of_speech` (long, more readable in prose); the spec author assumed schema-name parity that didn't exist. Future-defense: any sprint touching a DB column must `grep` migration files first to lock the canonical name. Added to gates as "Gate 11.5 — column-name source-of-truth check before write." **Audit hotfix count: 23 → 24.** Refs Sprint 10.1 migration 049 (canonical column names), Sprint 10.5 Phase 1 PR #204.
- Sprint 10.5 Phase 1 — **Personalized D1 from user vocab bank — storage + generation pipeline (Area 2, Issue #8 — "two separate apps" gap).** D1 fill-blank has historically been admin-authored (`vocabulary_exercises` table) — a generic pool everyone shares, disconnected from each learner's captured vocab. Sprint 10.0 discovery flagged this as Issue #8 ("two separate apps"). Sprint 10.5 wires D1 to the user's confirmed vocab bank so each learner practices exercises generated from their own words. Andy locked 5 questions on the discovery review (Q1=B AI generation at confirm time / Q2=A fill-blank only / Q3=A SRS-driven selection / Q4=B admin pool fallback / Q5=A 10 questions/session @ 70% due + 30% new). **Scope split (Andy authorized: "ship pipeline + admin fallback first, prompt tuning Sprint 10.5.x"):** Phase 1 (THIS PR) ships storage + AI generation + confirm hook + backfill script — the data layer that populates `user_d1_questions`. Phase 2 (Sprint 10.5.1) flips the user-facing surface — session endpoint mixes personalized + admin_fallback per Q5 ratio, attempt handler validates personalized answers against `target_answer` + `acceptable_variants`, frontend renders source label + free-text input for personalized rows. The split lets Andy verify generation quality in the DB before flipping the user surface; mirrors the Sprint 10.2 → 10.2.1 pattern. **Schema (migration 052).** `CREATE TABLE user_d1_questions (id UUID, user_id UUID REFERENCES users(id), vocabulary_id UUID REFERENCES user_vocabulary(id) ON DELETE CASCADE, context_sentence TEXT, blank_position_start/_end INTEGER, target_answer TEXT, acceptable_variants JSONB, hint TEXT, source_evidence_substring TEXT, generated_by TEXT, is_active BOOLEAN, attempt_count INTEGER, last_used_at TIMESTAMPTZ, created_at TIMESTAMPTZ, UNIQUE (user_id, vocabulary_id, context_sentence))`. Two indexes — `(user_id, is_active)` for the session hot path, `(vocabulary_id)` for backfill + cascade. RLS policy `user_id = auth.uid()` USING + WITH CHECK so users can only read/write their own questions. Idempotent (`IF NOT EXISTS` + `DROP POLICY IF EXISTS … CREATE POLICY`). FK uses project's `users(id)` not Supabase `auth.users(id)` per project convention (`.claude/skills/db-migrate/SKILL.md`). Schema spec falsification: spec asked for `auth.users(id)` but every project migration cited in the skill file references the project's own `users` table — went with project convention. **AI generator (`services/d1_question_generator.py`, NEW, ~310 LOC).** Two-tier fallback: Claude Haiku 4.5 (primary, same model as `vocab_extractor.py`) → Gemini 2.5 Flash (fallback, same model as `services/d1_content_gen.py` admin pool generator) → evidence-substring fallback (mask first occurrence of headword in user's original capture). `generate_d1_question(vocab_row) → dict | None`. System prompt asks for ONE new sentence in IELTS Part 1–3 register, 12–25 words, target word verbatim, no synonyms that give it away. Validation (`_validate_ai_payload`): target_answer matches headword (case-insensitive — tolerates morphological drift if headword still in sentence), sentence length 8–35 words (drift guard with slack vs the spec's 12–25 because models pad), blank positions computed via regex `\\b<target>\\b` (word-boundary anchored to skip "use" matching inside "used"), loose substring fallback for contractions. Acceptable variants lowercased, deduped, target word stripped from the variant list. Hint normalized to None when empty. Returns enriched dict with `blank_position_start/_end`, `generated_by` provenance tag (`haiku` | `gemini` | `fallback_evidence`), `source_evidence_substring` snapshot. Evidence fallback only fires if both AI calls fail AND evidence contains the headword — otherwise returns None so the caller logs and the backfill script picks up on next run. **Confirm hook (`routers/vocabulary_bank.py`).** `POST /api/vocabulary/bank/pending/{id}/confirm` and `POST /api/vocabulary/bank/pending/bulk-confirm` gained a `background_tasks: BackgroundTasks` parameter. After the `is_pending` flip, the endpoints schedule `_run_d1_generation_for_vocab(vocab_id)` as a FastAPI BackgroundTask — runs in the same process post-response, hides AI latency (~1–3s) from the caller. Helper fetches the vocab row via `supabase_admin` (service-role, bypasses RLS for trusted server-side write), calls `generate_d1_question`, INSERTs result. Fail-soft pattern: vocab lookup failures, AI generation failures, and DB insert failures all log a warning and return — the confirm response is success regardless of generation outcome. UNIQUE-violation on INSERT (re-fire or backfill race) is downgraded to DEBUG-level log via substring match `"duplicate" in str(e).lower() or "unique" in str(e).lower()`. Defensive guard: helper bails if the vocab row is archived or flipped back to pending between schedule and run (stale schedule, skip silently). **Backfill script (`scripts/backfill_d1_questions.py`, NEW, ~170 LOC).** `python -m scripts.backfill_d1_questions`. Fetches every alive confirmed vocab (`is_archived=false AND is_pending=false`) and every existing `user_d1_questions.vocabulary_id` in one shot, builds an in-memory set for O(1) skip lookups. For each vocab without a question: call generator, INSERT, log success. Rate limit: 100ms sleep between AI calls via module-level `_SLEEP_MS = 100` (tests monkeypatch to 0). Concurrent run protection: UNIQUE-violation on INSERT counts as `skipped_existing` not `errored` so re-run summaries stay coherent. Progress log every 10 iterations. Idempotent — re-run after a clean sweep reports `generated=0`. Parallel pattern with `backfill_lemma.py` (Sprint 10.1) and `backfill_mastery.py` (Sprint 10.2). **Tests (+14 net new):** `tests/test_d1_question_generator.py` — 9 unit tests covering: Haiku happy path (validates blank position computed from first occurrence), validation rejects sentences missing target, validation rejects out-of-range sentence length, acceptable variants normalized (lowercase + dedup + target stripped), Haiku-failure → Gemini-fail → evidence fallback chain, all-paths-fail returns None, empty headword short-circuits before AI call (defensive), Haiku invalid JSON falls through, Haiku strips ` ```json ... ``` ` markdown fences. Each test stubs `anthropic.Anthropic` with a `_FakeAnthropicClient` recording all `messages.create` calls so the test can also assert call count where relevant. `tests/test_backfill_d1_questions.py` — 3 tests: generates one question per alive vocab (asserts insert payload, `generated_by` provenance flows through), idempotent on second run (vocab with existing question row → 0 generator calls, 0 inserts), continues after generator returns None (mid-loop failure doesn't poison remaining items). `tests/test_vocab_pending.py` — 2 new scheduling tests + 5 existing confirm/bulk-confirm tests updated to pass `_FakeBackgroundTasks` shim: `test_confirm_schedules_d1_question_generation` (asserts exactly one `_run_d1_generation_for_vocab(vocab_id)` task queued), `test_bulk_confirm_schedules_one_generation_per_id` (3-ID payload with 1 foreign → 2 tasks queued for owned IDs only, all targeting the canonical helper). **Backend pytest: 994 passed / 23 skipped / 0 failed** (up from 980 baseline post-10.4 + 14 net new = 994). **Frontend: unchanged** — Phase 1 is backend-only. **Spec falsifications:** (36) Spec asked for `BackgroundTasks` schema with `acceptable_variants JSONB DEFAULT '[]'::jsonb` (PostgreSQL casting expression) — used `NOT NULL DEFAULT '[]'::jsonb` since the column is non-null in the spec semantics (an array is always present, may be empty). Matches the existing JSONB pattern in `users.feature_flags`. (37) Spec asked for `auth.users(id)` FK; project convention uses `users(id)` per the `db-migrate` SKILL. Verified by reading three recent migrations (049, 050, 051) — all reference `users(id)`. (38) Spec said "Question format: A — Fill-blank only (match current D1 UX)" but the actual current UX (`d1-exercise.js`) is MCQ (options array, local-grade against `ex.answer`). Sprint 10.5 Phase 1 doesn't ship session/attempt/frontend so this divergence is deferred to Phase 2 — the spec interpretation needs Andy review before Phase 2 starts: either personalized questions need AI-generated distractors (keep MCQ UX) or the frontend needs a free-text rendering path (matches spec's "Do NOT send target_answer to client"). Phase 1 schema supports both options. (39) `BackgroundTasks` runs in the same process post-response. Fine for ≤30s AI calls; if a future sprint introduces longer-running generation (multi-question batches, multimodal extraction), migration to a proper job queue (Celery, RQ, or Supabase Edge Functions) becomes load-bearing. Flagged for Sprint 10.7 reliability sweep. **Audit hotfix count: unchanged at 23** — Sprint 10.5 is foundation 5/9 of the Sprint 10.0 Option A roadmap, not a hotfix.
- Sprint 10.4.1-hotfix — **Pending-vocab panel light-mode contrast + Needs Review canonical `.vocab-card` adoption.** Smoke test of Sprint 10.4 (PR #202) flagged two visual bugs on `result.html` and the Needs Review tab. **Bug 1 diagnose**: the smoke-test hypothesis that the Sprint 10.4 CI fix (commit `18d97bd`) broke `.band-score` / bullet text light-mode rendering was FALSIFIED — that commit only touched the new `.pending-panel__*` / `.pending-card__*` rules at the bottom of result.css; `.ds-band-hero`, `.ds-band-value.band-*`, and `.result-feedback-list` cascade unchanged and resolve to readable tokens (`var(--av-error)` = `#B91C1C` on `var(--av-primary-soft)` light ≈ 9.3:1 contrast AAA). The actual light-mode bug introduced in Sprint 10.4 was the pending-vocab panel itself: `.pending-panel` used `--av-surface-card` (= `#FFFFFF` light) and `.pending-card` used `--av-surface-elevated` (also `#FFFFFF` light) → cards rendered invisible on the panel because parent + child shared the same surface. The `--av-border-subtle` (6% navy) card border was too faint to delineate them. **Fix**: panel lifted to `--av-surface-sunken` (light grey in light, deeper navy in dark) so cards on `--av-surface-card` visibly elevate; card border bumped to `--av-border-default` (12% navy) for readable delineation; `.pending-card__btn--drop` background changed from `--av-surface-elevated` (= card surface) to `transparent` so the button reads against the card outline + label color (`--av-text-secondary`) rather than blending into the white card. Dark-mode rendering unchanged (`--av-surface-sunken` = `#061021` and `--av-surface-card` = `#112236` already had separation). **Bug 2 audit**: Needs Review card (`/js/vocab-modules/needs-review.js` Sprint 10.1.5) shipped its own `.nr-card__*` primitive family in `css/needs-review.css` BEFORE the Sprint 9.3 my-vocab card primitives stabilized into `my-vocabulary.css`. Result: visual drift between Needs Review tab and the `source_type='needs_review'` rows surfacing in the My Vocab tab. Both tabs render the SAME backend data (`/api/vocabulary/bank/needs-review` and `GET /` with `source_type=needs_review`), but Needs Review used bespoke `.nr-card`, `.nr-card__original`, `.nr-card__suggestion`, `.nr-card__btn--fix`, `.nr-card__btn--dismiss` while my-vocab used the canonical `.vocab-card`, `.source-badge.badge-needs_review`, `.vocab-action--fixed`, `.vocab-action--skip`. **Refactor**: needs-review.js `cardHtml()` rewritten to emit `.vocab-card` with `<s>original</s> → suggestion` arrow header (preserves the Sprint 10.1.5 pedagogical visual), `<span class="source-badge badge-needs_review">Cần xem lại ⚠</span>` pill, source link via `<a class="vocab-action vocab-action--source">↗ nguồn</a>`, action buttons via `<button class="vocab-action vocab-action--fixed">✏️ Đã sửa, đưa lên flashcard</button>` and `<button class="vocab-action vocab-action--skip">🗑️ Bỏ qua</button>`. Body text uses `.mv-context` (italic muted) and `.mv-reason` (faint). Functional handlers untouched: `data-action="mark-fixed"` still hits POST `/{id}/mark-fixed` (server flips `source_type='needs_review' → 'manual'`); `data-action="dismiss"` still hits DELETE `/{id}` (soft-delete via `is_archived=true`). The bespoke `.nr-card*` block (~115 lines, lines 31–148 of needs-review.css) is DELETED — primitives now live in `my-vocabulary.css` which is already linked by vocabulary.html ahead of needs-review.css. The kept blocks in needs-review.css are `.needs-review-intro` (unique pedagogical banner) and `.nr-toast` (unique toast singleton). **No new CSS rules added.** The smoke-prompt phrasing "adopt `.mode-card` primitive" was reinterpreted: `.mode-card` is the dashboard-tile primitive (clickable feature card with hover-elevate transform), not a content card. The canonical primitive for vocab-item content cards is `.vocab-card`, which is what my-vocab uses and what needs-review now uses too. **Tests (7 net new)**: `tests/pending-vocab.test.mjs` gains a Sprint 10.4.1-hotfix describe block (4 pins): `.pending-panel` must use `--av-surface-sunken` (not `--av-surface-card`); `.pending-card` must use `--av-surface-card`; `.pending-card` border must use `--av-border-default`; `.pending-card__btn--drop` must use `background: transparent` + `--av-text-secondary` color. Plus a second describe block (3 pins) for the needs-review refactor: needs-review.css has zero `.nr-card*` selector rules; needs-review.js emits `.vocab-card` + `.source-badge.badge-needs_review` + `.vocab-action vocab-action--fixed` + `.vocab-action vocab-action--skip`; needs-review.js has zero `.nr-card__*` BEM emissions. Existing `tests/vocab-module-loader.test.mjs` "Needs Review card layout ships..." pin updated to match the new `.vocab-card` skeleton (`<s>${esc(original)}</s>` strikethrough + `data-lucide="arrow-right"` + canonical class names) instead of the retired `.nr-card__*` family. **Frontend node tests: 2642 passed / 0 failed** (+7 net new vs Sprint 10.4 baseline 2635). **Backend pytest: unchanged** — hotfix is frontend-only. **Audit hotfix count: 22 → 23.** **Spec falsifications**: (34) Token swap that resolves correctly in dark mode does NOT guarantee correct rendering in light mode — every `--av-surface-*` swap must verify parent/child surface tokens land on different greys in light mode (where `--av-surface-card` and `--av-surface-elevated` both equal `#FFFFFF`). The CI token-discipline gate only checks "uses tokens, not literals" — it doesn't check "tokens resolve to readable parent/child pairs". (35) "Adopt design system primitives" is only effective if the surface ships AFTER the primitives stabilize. Sprint 10.1.5 (Needs Review) shipped BEFORE Sprint 9.3 finalized the `.vocab-card` primitive family in my-vocabulary.css, so the bespoke `.nr-card*` family was created in good faith but became drift the moment the canonical primitive landed. - Sprint 10.4 — **Capture confirmation UI: pending staging + result.html confirmation panel (Area 1B, Issue #1 from Sprint 10.0 discovery).** Andy complaint #1: items auto-saved to bank without user confirmation; false positives only caught later via My Vocab triage (out-of-flow friction). Sprint 10.4 adds an in-session confirmation step — items capture as `is_pending=true`, the user confirms via a panel on `result.html`, then they flip into the bank. Pending items are invisible everywhere except the new `/pending` endpoints. **Schema (migration 051).** `ALTER TABLE user_vocabulary ADD is_pending BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT false, ADD pending_created_at TIMESTAMPTZ`. Partial index on `(user_id, is_pending, pending_created_at) WHERE is_pending = true` for fast pending-list reads + auto-commit cutoff scans. Idempotent (`IF NOT EXISTS` everywhere); no backfill — existing 46 alive items grandfather in via the column default. Column COMMENTs document the deprecation timeline (Sprint 10.6 drop, same pattern as `mastery_status` from Sprint 10.2). **Capture pipeline (`routers/grading.py`).** The `rows_to_insert` payload in `_run_vocab_extraction_bg` now adds `is_pending=true` + `pending_created_at=datetime.now(timezone.utc).isoformat()`. Lemma + guard logic untouched. Manual-add (`POST /api/vocabulary/bank/`) intentionally stays `is_pending=false` — typing it yourself is self-confirmation; the confirmation panel exists for AI-extracted captures specifically. **User-facing reads filter `is_pending=false`.** Sprint 10.4 grep'd every `.table("user_vocabulary").select(...)` in the user-facing path and added the filter: bank GET / stats / recent / recent-updates / needs-review / detail / export endpoints in `routers/vocabulary_bank.py`; flashcard due-queue + auto-stack count + topic list + uncategorized probe + struggling-vocab + preview/create stack `_apply_filter` helper + add-to-stack lookup + review-vocab check in `routers/flashcards.py`; D1 attempt's `target_vocab_id` lookup in `routers/exercises.py` (pending vocab can't feed SRS via D1 either); home dashboard widget in `services/dashboard_aggregator.py`; home counters in `services/student_home_aggregator.py`. Per-item action endpoints (PATCH / DELETE / accept / mark-fixed / skip / report) gained the filter too — pending items only reachable via the new `/pending/*` endpoints; calling a bank action on a pending vocab_id 404s. **Pending endpoints (new, `vocabulary_bank.py`).** `GET /api/vocabulary/bank/pending` — lists the user's pending items, newest first; runs a lazy 24h auto-commit cleanup at the top so stale rows never appear. `POST /api/vocabulary/bank/pending/{id}/confirm` — flips `is_pending=false` + clears `pending_created_at`. `POST /api/vocabulary/bank/pending/{id}/drop` — soft-delete (`is_archived=true` AND clears pending — leaving both true would create a phantom row invisible everywhere). `POST /api/vocabulary/bank/pending/bulk-confirm` — body `{ids: list[str]}`, validates ownership via `user_id` filter on the UPDATE (foreign IDs in the payload silently no-op, no info leak). Andy Q4 lock: "Keep all" is the only batch action — no Drop all endpoint. **Auto-commit (Andy Q3 lock).** Discovery step confirmed no scheduler (APScheduler/Celery/etc) is running in `backend/main.py` or `services/`. Sprint 10.4 implements the 24h auto-commit as a lazy cleanup inside `GET /pending`: `_auto_commit_stale_pending(sb, user_id)` runs an UPDATE WHERE `pending_created_at < now() - interval '24 hours'` AND `is_pending=true` before the SELECT. Cost: one extra UPDATE per GET when stale items exist (negligible). Drift risk: a user who never visits the pending page leaves items pending indefinitely — acceptable for daily-active users, flagged for re-evaluation if adoption shows longer absences. Lifted via module constant `_PENDING_AUTO_COMMIT_HOURS = 24`. **Frontend (`frontend/js/pending-vocab.js`, NEW).** ES module exporting `mount(container, opts)`. Fetches `GET /pending`; if the list is empty, the container stays hidden (Andy spec § 8 — no empty-state UI). Otherwise renders a `.pending-panel` with header (title, subtitle, "Giữ tất cả" batch button), one `.pending-card` per item (headword, definition, quoted context, AI feedback, "Giữ" + "Bỏ" buttons), and a "💡 Tự động lưu sau 24h..." footer. Per-card actions use the Sprint 10.2.1 optimistic-update pattern: card fades synchronously (`pending-card--leaving` class flips `opacity: 0 + translateX(8px)` via CSS transition), POST fires in the background, on success the card is removed from the DOM (panel auto-hides when the last card leaves via `maybeUnmountIfEmpty`), on error `restoreCard` un-fades and `flashToast('Không lưu được, thử lại nhé.', 'error')` surfaces. Bulk-confirm fades all visible cards together then POSTs the IDs in one batch. Module-level idempotency guard via `data-pending-mounted` on the container — calling `mount()` twice short-circuits the second call. **`frontend/pages/result.html` integration.** New `<div id="pending-vocab-mount" class="hidden">` between the per-question accordion and the action-button row. The inline result-page script dynamic-imports `../js/pending-vocab.js` after the result data loads (the `.then(mount).catch(warn)` chain is non-fatal — if the import fails the panel stays hidden and the rest of the page works). **CSS (`frontend/css/result.css`).** `.pending-panel`, `.pending-panel__head/__title/__subtitle/__keep-all/__notice`, `.pending-card`, `.pending-card__head/__headword/__def/__context/__reason/__actions/__btn--keep/__btn--drop`, `.pending-card--leaving` transition class. Token-bound via `--av-surface-card`, `--av-text-muted`, etc. so the dark/cream theme variants both work. **Tests (24 net new).** Backend `tests/test_vocab_pending.py` — 13 router-layer pins: bank GET hides pending; `/pending` lists pending only; archived rows excluded; confirm flips flag + 404 on already-confirmed + 404 on foreign user; drop archives row; 404 on already-confirmed for drop; bulk-confirm flips all owned + ignores foreign + empty payload; auto-commit fires at 25h + does NOT fire at 23h (off-by-one pin). The test fixture extends the Sprint 10.2/10.3 mock builder with `.lt()` (cutoff comparison), `.in_()` (bulk-confirm), AND a deferred-execute pattern so `.update(payload).eq(...).eq(...).lt(...).execute()` chains apply WHERE clauses correctly (Gate 9.6 — Sprint 10.1.5-hotfix lesson). **Gate 9.5 stale-pin scrub.** `tests/test_dashboard_init.py:_vocab()`, `tests/test_needs_review_redefined.py:_vocab()`, `tests/test_student_home_aggregator.py:_seed_vocab()` fixture helpers gained `is_pending=False` defaults so the predicate-filter mocks keep their canned rows visible. Without this, the 15 tests that relied on the dashboard widget / home counter / auto-stack listing return values would have failed silently when the new `.eq("is_pending", False)` filter dropped fixture rows that lacked the column. Frontend `tests/pending-vocab.test.mjs` — 10 sentinel pins: module exports `mount(container, opts)`, empty-list early-return, Keep/Drop/Keep-all data-actions wired, Vietnamese copy strings present (no English bleed), optimistic fade before await ordering, rollback path restores card + flashToast, bulk-confirm POSTs the visible IDs, result.html ships the mount target hidden by default, result.html dynamic-imports the module, result.css ships the `.pending-panel` + `.pending-card--leaving` rules. **Backend pytest: 980 passed / 23 skipped / 0 failed** (up from 967 baseline post-10.3.1; +13 net new pending tests). **Frontend node tests: 162 passed / 0 failed** (+10 net new). **Audit hotfix count unchanged at 22** — Sprint 10.4 is foundation 4/9 of the Sprint 10.0 Option A roadmap. **Spec falsifications:** (31) "Add confirmation step" sounds UX-only but touches *every* bank read path — 42 SELECT sites surveyed, ~20 needed the new filter, the rest (admin / dedup / grading existing-headword lookup) intentionally skip the filter so dedup still catches pending and admin sees full data. (32) "Drop = hard delete" considered then rejected: drop = `is_archived=true` (soft) preserves evidence trail for analytics + an eventual undo path via the existing `POST /{id}/restore` endpoint. (33) Auto-commit via background scheduler considered then rejected: no scheduler running in `main.py` / services; lazy-check inside `GET /pending` is the right zero-infra fit. The drift trade-off (items > 24h sit pending until next visit) is acceptable for daily-active users and noted as a future migration target if adoption suggests longer absences.
- Sprint 10.3.1-hotfix (this PR) — **Flip D1 wrong-rating `'hard' → 'again'` (SM-2 semantics correction).** Sprint 10.3 PR #200 locked Q4 rating=`'hard'` for wrong-first-attempt on the assumption that `'hard'` was a "softer demote" than `'again'`. That assumption is wrong per SM-2 canonical semantics: `'hard'` is *slower growth* (×1.2 from prior interval), not demotion at all; `'again'` is the actual reset (interval→0, lapse_count++). Layering `'hard'` on top of floor=7 cancelled the floor's purpose for mastered cards — wrong on `interval=25` grew to ~30 instead of clamping to 7, and `lapse_count` stayed at 0 so mastery never flipped. The PR description flagged this divergence at ship time; the pedagogical sanity check in the Sprint 10.3 spec (interval=25 → 7, lapses+1) failed silently. **Fix:** 1-line change in `routers/exercises.py` `submit_d1_attempt`: `srs_rating = "good" if is_correct else "again"`. Floor=7 now acts as the single safeguard at the right layer — `'again'` resets interval to 0, floor clamps up to 7, `lapse_count` bumps to 1, mastery flips to `'learning'` via the Sprint 10.2 threshold derivation. **Spec falsification 30:** when pinning a config value (e.g. Q4 rating), verify against the canonical algorithm reference *before* locking. Q4 was locked on English-language intuition ("hard sounds gentler than again"), not on the SM-2 formula in `services/srs.py`. Pre-work § 15 addendum for future sprints: cite the algorithm source when locking rating/policy params. **Tests (3 updated, 0 net new).** `tests/test_exercises_d1_srs.py` renamed `test_first_wrong_attempt_upserts_srs_with_hard_rating_and_floor` → `test_first_wrong_attempt_upserts_srs_with_again_rating_and_floor`; assertion `resp["srs_rating"] == "hard"` → `"again"`; new pin `row["lapse_count"] == 1` (was implicitly 0 with `'hard'`). `test_wrong_attempt_on_mastered_card_does_not_demote_below_floor` renamed → `test_wrong_attempt_on_mastered_card_demotes_to_floor_with_lapse`; expected `interval_days == 30` → `== 7`, gained `lapse_count == 1` pin, gained column-sync `{mastery_status: "learning"}` pin (the canonical pedagogical case now passes — pre-10.3.1 it would have asserted `mastered`). Frontend `d1-exercise.js` `renderSrsIndicator` docstring + `tests/d1-srs-indicator.test.mjs` doc string mention `'again'` instead of `'hard'`; runtime branch (`srs_rating === 'good'` else "Lưu ý") covers any non-good rating so no JS-runtime change was needed. **Backend pytest: 967 passed / 23 skipped / 0 failed** (no count change; same 22 D1-SRS + SRS algorithm tests, semantics flipped). **Audit hotfix count: 21 → 22.**
- Sprint 10.3 (this PR) — **D1 → SRS feedback loop with first-attempt-only + gated demotion floor (Area 3B, Issue #7 from Sprint 10.0 discovery).** Pre-10.3, a correct D1 fill-blank attempt only logged to `vocabulary_exercise_attempts` (append-only) — the strongest pedagogical signal in the system (productive recall: write the word in context) was discarded before it could feed `flashcard_reviews`. Sprint 10.3 wires the outcome into SRS with two safeguards that trade marginal signal for vastly better adoption (Andy Q1–Q4 lock). **Safeguard 1 (first-attempt-only, Q2).** A COUNT-before-insert query on `(user_id, exercise_id)` determines whether this attempt is the user's first on this exercise. Only the first attempt fires SRS — retries log but skip the update. Anti-gaming: prevents "spam-retry until rating recovers". Implementation note (spec falsification 29): the count MUST run before the attempt INSERT or the just-inserted row gets counted; we use the user-scoped client so RLS gates the query. **Safeguard 2 (gated demotion floor=7, Q3).** Wrong answers map to `rating='hard'` (Q4 — softer than `'again'`); the SRS update passes `floor=7` so any wrong answer leaves `interval_days >= 7`. The floor only *raises* under-floor intervals; never lowers an interval already above 7. Combined with the SM-2 'hard' growth-factor (×1.2), a single wrong answer on a mastered card cannot demote it below the 1-week buffer. **`backend/services/srs.py` — new `floor` param.** `update_srs(review, rating, floor: int = 0)`. Default 0 preserves pre-10.3 behaviour for flashcard-review session callers; D1 path passes `floor=7`. Floor applied AFTER the SM-2 step but BEFORE the absolute `_INTERVAL_CAP=36500` clamp. Pure function, no DB I/O — caller still owns the upsert. **`backend/services/mastery.py` — `sync_mastery_column()` extracted (Gate 3 drift fix).** The column-sync logic Sprint 10.2.1-hotfix inlined in `routers/vocabulary_bank.py` PATCH is lifted into the service module so the new D1 path and the existing PATCH path share one source. Same fail-soft contract: log WARN on Supabase exception; `backfill_mastery.py` reconciles. `vocabulary_bank.py` PATCH refactored to call the helper. **`backend/routers/exercises.py` — D1 attempt handler.** New module-level constant `_D1_SRS_FLOOR_DAYS = 7` (Andy Q3 lock). New helper `_apply_d1_srs_update(sb, user_id, vocab_id, rating)` — fetches existing `flashcard_reviews` row (defaults to SM-2 init values when none), runs `update_srs(prev, rating, floor=7)`, upserts the result, then calls `sync_mastery_column`. Returns True on success. Handler-level logic: SELECT also includes `target_vocab_id`; COUNT-before-insert determines first-attempt; skip conditions check `target_vocab_id IS NOT NULL` + vocab not archived + vocab row visible to the user. Response shape gains `srs_updated: bool` + `srs_rating: 'good' | 'hard' | None`. Pre-10.3 frontends ignore unknown fields; post-10.3 d1-exercise.js renders an indicator. **`frontend/js/d1-exercise.js`.** `postAttemptWithRetry()` now returns the parsed JSON body (or `null`) instead of a bare boolean so the caller can read the SRS outcome. `onAnswerClick()` chains `.then(data => renderSrsIndicator(data)).finally(...)` after the fire-and-forget POST. NEW `renderSrsIndicator(data)`: early-returns when `srs_updated` is false; otherwise picks "✓ Đã ghi nhận vào ôn tập" (`srs_rating='good'`) or "📝 Lưu ý cho lần ôn tới" (else). Replaces any prior indicator via `.querySelector('.d1-srs-indicator').remove()` so a fast clicker can't stack. **`frontend/pages/d1-exercise.html`.** Inline `<style>` adds `.d1-srs-indicator { margin-top: 8px; font-size: 12px; opacity: 0.78; … }` — muted styling so it doesn't compete with the existing correct/wrong feedback banner. **Tests (21 net new).** `tests/test_srs_algorithm.py` — 5 floor pins: lifts under-floor interval, doesn't lower already-higher, lifts 'again' zero to floor, 'good' standard unchanged, `floor=0` default byte-equivalent to pre-10.3 call shape. NEW `tests/test_exercises_d1_srs.py` — 10 router-layer tests: first-correct → SRS good upsert, first-wrong → SRS hard upsert with floor clamp, wrong on mastered card doesn't drop below 7, second attempt (correct or wrong) skips SRS but still logs the attempt, null `target_vocab_id` / archived vocab / missing vocab row all short-circuit cleanly, column sync via shared helper fires the user_vocabulary UPDATE, response shape carries `srs_updated`/`srs_rating` on every path (pre-10.3 compat). NEW `frontend/tests/d1-srs-indicator.test.mjs` — 6 sentinel pins: JSON body parse + return, `.then(renderSrsIndicator)` chain, early-return when `srs_updated` false, label branching on `srs_rating === 'good'`, replace-don't-stack helper call, `.d1-srs-indicator` CSS rule present. **Gate 9.6 mock builder upgrade.** The D1 router tests stand up a multi-table `_Client` extending the Sprint 10.2 pattern with `.insert()` recording for `vocabulary_exercise_attempts` and a `.eq()`-no-op chain. The rate-limit decorator runs at import time and lazy-imports `routers.auth.get_supabase_user` — the test fixture patches `routers.auth.get_supabase_user` AND `routers.exercises.get_supabase_user` AND replaces `services.rate_limit.enforce_exercise_rate_limit` with a no-op so the decorator doesn't hit Supabase. **Backend pytest: 967 passed / 23 skipped / 0 failed** (up from 952 baseline post-10.2.1; +15 net new). **Frontend node tests: 152 passed / 0 failed** (+6 net new). **Audit hotfix count unchanged at 21** — Sprint 10.3 is foundation 3/9 of the Option A roadmap, not audit.
- Sprint 10.2.1-hotfix (this PR) — **PATCH syncs deprecated column + optimistic button flip.** Sprint 10.2 production smoke surfaced two design gaps. **Gap 1 — column drift.** The PATCH handler upserted `flashcard_reviews` (the new source of truth) but never wrote back to `user_vocabulary.mastery_status`. Sprint 10.2's design treated the column as write-once-on-capture / sync-via-backfill-script, but admin Table Editor and direct SQL clients bypass the API and saw stale values — 7/29 cards diverged within the first day. Forcing the operator to run `backfill_mastery` after every batch of user clicks is fragile. **Fix:** one extra UPDATE in the PATCH handler immediately after the SRS upsert, writing the derived value. Failure is non-fatal (logged WARN; backfill still reconciles). Column stays deprecated *for reads* (bank GET still derives from `flashcard_reviews`); drop remains scheduled for Sprint 10.6. **Gap 2 — slow button feedback.** Button click awaited PATCH → awaited GET `/stats` → re-rendered list. Perceived latency ~800ms on prod. **Fix:** optimistic update — flip `item.mastery_status` synchronously, update stat counter in place via new `_shiftStatCounter(from, to)` helper, `renderList()` before fetching. PATCH fires in the background; on response, reconcile only if the server-derived status disagrees (rare — would require a server-side rule change). On error, roll back the optimistic flip + counter shift + `flashToast('Không cập nhật được, thử lại nhé.', 'error')`. Server stays authoritative as tie-breaker; happy path no longer blocks on the network. **Backend changes (3 lines + comment block).** `routers/vocabulary_bank.py` PATCH handler: post-upsert column sync wrapped in try/except — the SRS write is the API contract; the column write is best-effort. **Frontend changes.** `js/vocab-modules/my-vocab.js` `toggleMastery()` rewritten — optimistic flip → local counter math → background PATCH → reconcile/rollback. `_shiftStatCounter()` reads `[data-stat="mastered"]` and `[data-stat="learning"]` selectors, updates `textContent` synchronously. Removed `await loadStats()` from the toggle path (the call survives in the initial load + after manual-add). **Tests (9 net new).** Backend: `test_patch_mastered_true_syncs_user_vocabulary_column`, `test_patch_mastered_false_syncs_user_vocabulary_column`, `test_patch_column_sync_failure_does_not_break_response` (fail-soft pin — Supabase update raising must not break the API response). Gate 9.5 scrub: existing `test_patch_mastered_true_upserts_srs_at_threshold` assertion `"PATCH must NOT write user_vocabulary"` flipped to clarify that flashcard_reviews is the PRIMARY write and the column UPDATE is a secondary sync verified by the new dedicated tests. 404 ownership test gained `client.updates == []` symmetry check. NEW `frontend/tests/my-vocab-optimistic-mastery.test.mjs` — 6 sentinel-style pins: optimistic assignment happens BEFORE the await, `loadStats()` is not called on the toggle path, payload is `{mastered}` not legacy `{mastery_status: ...}`, catch block has both rollback + `flashToast('...', 'error')`, success path reconciles via `resp.mastery_status !== optimisticStatus`, `_shiftStatCounter` helper exists and uses the canonical stat selectors. Source-string extractor (`_extractFunctionBody`) matches the existing `vocab-module-loader.test.mjs` sentinel pattern — no jsdom, no module loader. **Backend pytest: 952 passed / 23 skipped / 0 failed** (up from 949 post-10.2; +3 net new). **Frontend node tests: 146 passed / 0 failed** (+6 net new). **Audit hotfix count: 20 → 21.** Spec falsification 28: "Deprecated column = don't write to it" is a false dichotomy. Pragmatic deprecation = stop *reading*, keep *writing* until drop sprint. Otherwise admin tools + direct SQL clients drift silently.
- Sprint 10.2 (this PR) — **Mastery–SRS unification: SRS state is single source of truth (Area 3A, Issue #6 from Sprint 10.0 discovery).** Pre-10.2, `user_vocabulary.mastery_status` was a manual user toggle decoupled from SRS state — a card could be `mastered` AND have `lapse_count=5` simultaneously, two parallel models of "knows this word" that never synced. Sprint 10.2 collapses the two models: `flashcard_reviews` is canonical; `mastery_status` is derived. **Threshold (Andy Q1 lock, 2026-05-15):** `mastered := interval_days >= 21 AND lapse_count == 0 AND review_count >= 3`. Each clause guards a distinct failure mode — interval alone is fragile (lucky-guess SM-2 jumps); review_count gates real engagement; lapse_count demotes anything the user has ever forgotten. **Backend.** NEW `backend/services/mastery.py` — single `derive_mastery_status(srs_state) -> str` utility shared by the bank GET path, the PATCH handler response shape, and the backfill script (centralised so the three surfaces can't drift). NEW migration `050_mastery_srs_derivation.sql` — `COMMENT ON COLUMN user_vocabulary.mastery_status` marks it DEPRECATED with the drop scheduled for Sprint 10.6. Column kept physically present during the deprecation window so admin Table Editor reads and direct SQL queries don't see stale data; `scripts/backfill_mastery.py` (NEW) keeps it in sync by walking alive vocab + writing derived values back. **`backend/routers/vocabulary_bank.py`** — every read endpoint (`GET /`, `GET /needs-review`, `GET /{vocab_id}`, `GET /stats`, `GET /recent`) now fetches `flashcard_reviews` via the new `_fetch_srs_lookup(sb, user_id)` helper and applies `_apply_derived_mastery()` per row. The `?status=` filter operates on the DERIVED value, not the stale column, so a future column drift can't silently filter out rows whose SRS state has diverged. **PATCH endpoint reshaped (Q2 — Option C, keep button, write SRS).** `VocabUpdateStatusRequest` body changed from `{mastery_status: str}` to `{mastered: bool}` — the verb-state name nudges callers toward "this writes SRS, not a column". Mastered upsert recipe: `interval_days=21, lapse_count=0, review_count=max(existing,3), ease_factor=max(existing,2.5), next_review_at=now+21d, last_reviewed_at=now`. Unmark recipe preserves `ease_factor` + `last_reviewed_at` (we don't fabricate a forgetting event — unmark is a triage gesture). 404 ownership gate kept; upsert uses `on_conflict='user_id,vocabulary_id'` against the existing UNIQUE constraint. **Frontend.** `frontend/js/vocab-modules/my-vocab.js` button label flipped from "Mastered/Learning" English status to "Đã thuộc ✓ / Đánh dấu đã thuộc" Vietnamese action. `title` attr added: "Tự động cập nhật khi bạn ôn tập đều" — gentle nudge that mastery auto-updates from SRS, the toggle isn't an arbitrary override. PATCH payload changed to `{mastered: bool}`; the handler trusts the server's derived `mastery_status` in the response (no local guessing). Pill filter ("Learning" / "Mastered") unchanged — data fed in is already SRS-derived. **Tests (22 net new).** NEW `tests/test_mastery.py` (8 tests) pinning the derivation contract per clause + threshold-constant exposure for the PATCH handler. NEW `tests/test_vocab_bank_mastery_derivation.py` (9 tests) — GET derives even when column stale, status filter respects derived value, PATCH writes flashcard_reviews not user_vocabulary, mastered-true preserves higher existing review_count + ease_factor, mastered-false doesn't fabricate a lapse, 404 ownership gate, stats counter pin. NEW `tests/test_backfill_mastery.py` (5 tests) — stale-mastered → learning flip, stale-learning → mastered flip, in-sync rows skipped (no writes), idempotent second-run, empty-table no-op. **Gate 9.6 mock builder.** Sprint 10.1.5-hotfix lesson formalised: the existing `_FilterRecordingBuilder` in `test_vocab_skip.py` gained table-name routing so the new `flashcard_reviews` query path doesn't crash on the old user-vocabulary-only fixture shape. New tests build a richer `_Client` supporting `.upsert(on_conflict=...)` + `.update(row).eq(...)` chains. **Gate 9.5 stale-assertion scrub.** `tests/test_rls_vocab_integration.py:99` writes `{mastery_status: "mastered"}` directly to the table (bypasses API) — kept as-is because the column still exists during deprecation and the test is about RLS policy, not API contract. Fixture defaults of `"mastery_status": "learning"` in `test_vocab_skip.py` / `test_grading_vocab_filter.py` / `test_student_home_aggregator.py` stay correct because the capture pipeline still populates the column on insert. **Backend pytest: 949 passed / 23 skipped / 0 failed** (up from 927 baseline post-10.1; +22 net new tests). **Audit hotfix count unchanged at 20** — Sprint 10.2 is foundation 2/9 of the Sprint 10.0 Option A roadmap, not audit.
- Sprint 10.1.2-hotfix (this PR) — **Real Railway build fix: `.python-version` at repo root (Railpack v0.23.0, not Nixpacks).** Sprint 10.1.1-hotfix added `nixPkgs = ["python312"]` to `backend/nixpacks.toml`, expecting Railway to honour it. The next deploy still failed on the same blis cc-compile error. Build log inspection revealed the real builder: `using build driver railpack-v0.23.0` (line 4), then `python │ 3.13.13 │ railpack default (3.13)` (line 14). **Railway 2026 default is Railpack, not Nixpacks** — Nixpacks is legacy/deprecated for new services and Railpack ignores `nixpacks.toml` silently. So 10.1.1's pin was a no-op the whole time. **Real fix:** add `.python-version` file at the repo root containing `3.12`. Railpack reads via mise (in this order: `RAILPACK_PYTHON_VERSION` env var → `.python-version` file → `.tool-versions` → `mise.toml` → default 3.13), so a 4-byte file at repo root short-circuits the cascade before it falls through to the 3.13 default. Choice of `3.12` (major.minor) over `3.12.5` (patch-pinned) is deliberate: mise resolves major.minor to the latest patch with a precompiled binary, avoiding the "no precompiled python found" failure mode if a specific patch hasn't shipped a binary yet. **What stays:** `backend/nixpacks.toml` is kept verbatim (no-op under Railpack but insurance if Andy ever flips the service back to Nixpacks). `requirements.txt` and the `spacy==3.8.0` pin are untouched. **What I learned (Spec falsification 26+):** before pinning any version on Railway, read the first 20 lines of the build log to identify the active builder family (`railpack` vs `nixpacks` vs `buildpacks` vs `Dockerfile`). Pattern: build-tool family identification BEFORE version pinning. **Audit hotfix count UNCHANGED at 20** — 10.1.2 is an extension of the same incident as 10.1.1 (the parent 10.1 deploy never reached Railway green); per the standing rule, a hotfix that re-attempts a failed hotfix doesn't double-count.
- Sprint 10.1.1-hotfix (this PR) — **Railway build fix: pin Python 3.12 in nixpacks (blis pre-built wheels).** Andy's first deploy of PR #195 to Railway surfaced a build failure during the `pip install -r requirements.txt` step: `cc` failed compiling `blis` (the BLAS backend that spaCy → thinc pulls in transitively). Root cause: nixpacks' Python auto-detection landed on Python 3.13 — for which PyPI does not yet ship pre-built wheels for blis at the `spacy==3.8.0` / `thinc==8.x` pin we picked in Sprint 10.1. With no wheel available, pip falls through to a from-source compile that needs gcc and exhausts Railway's build container. Andy's directive ruled out two alternatives: (1) downgrading spaCy (10.1's lemma quality target depends on the 3.8.x model + rules) and (2) adding `gcc` to nixpacks (slow build, larger image, treats the symptom not the cause). **Fix:** add `nixPkgs = ["python312"]` to `[phases.setup]` in `backend/nixpacks.toml`. Python 3.12 has the full pre-built wheel chain (`blis` → `thinc` → `spacy` → `en_core_web_sm`) on PyPI, so the install is fast and the deployed image stays lean. The `[phases.install]` block is unchanged — `python` resolves to the 3.12 binary now that setup pinned it, and the `spacy download en_core_web_sm` step runs against the 3.12 venv. **Local verify deferred:** the dev machine doesn't have a 3.12 toolchain installed (only 3.11 + 3.13); Railway is the canonical verification surface for this fix. **Audit hotfix count: 19 → 20** (Sprint 10.1.1-hotfix is a deploy-time build fix, counted per the standing rule that build/CI hotfixes shipped in the same PR as their parent foundation sprint still increment the audit count).
- Sprint 10.1 (this PR) — **Server-side lemmatization foundation (1/9 of Option A roadmap).** Implements the first foundation sprint from the Sprint 10.0 discovery audit. spaCy `en_core_web_sm` adds canonical lemma + POS to every captured vocab item; Guard 6 gains a lemma-equality primary check that catches irregular-form duplicates (ran/run, went/go, was/be) that the pre-10.1 same-root + Levenshtein heuristics miss. **Schema (migration 049 — dual-write window).** Adds 4 columns to `user_vocabulary`: `surface_form TEXT` (verbatim user form, mirrors `headword` at capture time), `lemma TEXT` (spaCy lemma, lowercase), `pos TEXT` (universal POS — VERB/NOUN/ADJ/...), `lemma_version INTEGER DEFAULT 1` (schema-side rule-set version for future re-walks). Partial index `idx_user_vocabulary_user_lemma ON (user_id, lemma) WHERE lemma IS NOT NULL AND is_archived = false` keeps the lemma-equality dedup query O(log n). Legacy `headword` column + its UNIQUE constraint preserved — dual-write so Sprint 10.2 (UNIQUE-constraint flip to (user_id, lemma)) can land independently. **Lemmatizer service (`backend/services/lemmatizer.py`).** Thread-safe lazy singleton — spaCy loads on first call (~12 MB on disk, ~30 MB in memory after `disable=["parser","ner"]`). `lemmatize(surface) → (lemma, pos)` whitespace-trims and lowercases the input; multi-word inputs return the surface verbatim with the POS of the first content-bearing token (idioms must not be split per-token). `lemma_version() → int` returns the current rule-set version (bump on spaCy major upgrade or idiom-handling change; the backfill script compares stored versions and re-walks stale rows). `requirements.txt` pins `spacy==3.8.0` with a comment about the separate model install; `nixpacks.toml` adds `python -m spacy download en_core_web_sm` to the install phase so Railway cold-starts succeed. **Guard 6 (`backend/services/vocab_guards.py`).** `run_all_guards()` signature gains two backward-compatible optional params: `existing_lemmas: list[str] | None = None` and `new_lemma: str | None = None`. When both are provided, lemma-equality (case-insensitive, None-safe) runs FIRST and emits `guard_6_lemma_duplicate` on a hit. On miss — or when either param is None — the pre-10.1 3-heuristic block (same-root prefix ≥6, Levenshtein ≤ 2, semantic clusters) still runs and emits `guard_6_levenshtein_duplicate`. Pre-10.1 callers that don't pass the lemma params see byte-identical behaviour. **Capture pipeline (`backend/routers/grading.py`).** The `existing_headwords` lookup now also selects `lemma`; both lists feed `run_all_guards()`. Inside the persist loop, `lemmatize(headword)` runs BEFORE the guards (fail-soft — spaCy errors log a WARN and fall through to `(None, None, None)` so the legacy heuristic dedup still gates the row). Insert payload carries all 4 dual-write columns alongside `headword`. After a successful guard pass, `new_lemma` is appended to `existing_lemmas` so the next item in the same extraction can dedup against it. **Manual add (`backend/routers/vocabulary_bank.py`).** POST `/api/vocabulary/bank` follows the same fail-soft lemmatize-before-insert pattern; the manual surface and the AI-capture surface stay schema-consistent. **Backfill (`backend/scripts/backfill_lemma.py`).** Idempotent retro-fill via Supabase admin client — selects alive rows where `lemma IS NULL OR lemma_version < current_version`, per-row try/except so one bad row can't poison the run, summary log at exit (`processed/updated/skipped/errored`). Operator runs once after migration 049 lands: `cd backend && python -m scripts.backfill_lemma`. **Tests.** NEW `tests/test_lemmatizer.py` — 7 live spaCy tests gated by `@_skip_if_no_model` (probes `spacy.load()` at module init; skipped locally when the model isn't installed, runs green on Railway / CI where nixpacks installs it) covering running→run, ran→run, was→be, phenomena→phenomenon, multi-word idiom preservation, case insensitivity, idempotence; 5 wrapper-logic tests via monkeypatched `_get_nlp()` covering empty/whitespace handling, strip+lowercase preprocessing, multi-word surface preservation, and `lemma_version() ≥ 1`. NEW `tests/test_vocab_guards_lemma.py` — 11 tests pinning Guard 6 lemma-primary contract: irregular past-tense / gerund dedup, case-insensitive comparison, walk-the-list dedup, None-safe handling for legacy NULL-lemma rows, fallback-to-legacy when `new_lemma=None`, fallback when `existing_lemmas=[]`, fully-backward-compat call shape, legacy-fires-after-lemma-miss for typo dedup, distinct-lemma clean pass. UPDATED `tests/test_grading_vocab_filter.py` — persist-loop replay now mirrors the dual-write shape (`surface_form` + `lemma` + `pos` + `lemma_version` alongside `headword`); 2 new tests pin column presence and end-to-end lemma correctness (ran→run, gated on local spaCy availability via pytest.skip). **Backend pytest 927 passed / 23 skipped / 0 failed** (up from 910 pre-Sprint-10.1; 17 net new tests pinned). **Audit hotfix count unchanged at 19** (Sprint 10.1 is foundation, not audit).
- Sprint 10.1.5-hotfix (this PR) — **Backend pytest realignment to Sprint 10.1.5 capture-re-architecture intent.** CI on PR #194 surfaced 4 backend pytest failures after the Sprint 10.1.5 capture re-architecture landed. The failures were stale Sprint 6.0 tests that pinned the OLD behaviour (`needs_review` NOT persisted) — exactly the contract Sprint 10.1.5 deliberately reversed. A GitHub bug-analysis bot proposed reverting `_PERSISTED_SOURCE_TYPES = {'used_well', 'upgrade_suggested', 'needs_review'}` back to the pre-10.1.5 2-element set, which would have undone Andy-approved Sprint 10.1.5 intent. Sprint 10.1.5-hotfix instead realigns the tests to the new contract: needs_review IS persisted at the write layer; the main-bank list endpoint default-excludes it at the read layer via `.neq("source_type", "needs_review")`; the dedicated `GET /api/vocabulary/bank/needs-review` endpoint surfaces the items for the Needs Review tab. **Test changes (2 files, 4 fixes):** **(a) `backend/tests/test_grading_vocab_filter.py`** — module-docstring header updated to document the Sprint 6.0 → 10.1.5 evolution (was: "Sprint 6.0 explicitly drops needs_review"; now: "Sprint 10.1.5 re-enables persistence + routes to dedicated tab"). Three tests retargeted: (i) `test_persisted_source_types_constant_excludes_needs_review` renamed to `test_persisted_source_types_constant_includes_needs_review`; assertion flipped from `assert "needs_review" NOT in _PERSISTED_SOURCE_TYPES` → `assert "needs_review" IN _PERSISTED_SOURCE_TYPES`; failure-message updated to point future engineers at the 3 surfaces that expect needs_review to exist (list-endpoint default-exclude filter, Needs Review surface endpoint, frontend needs-review.js module). (ii) `test_needs_review_items_skipped` renamed to `test_needs_review_items_persisted_to_needs_review_surface`; assertion flipped from `assert rows == []` → `assert len(rows) == 2 + all source_type == 'needs_review' + suggestion field preserved` (the suggestion field carries the AI's correction text for the original→suggestion card layout in the frontend module). (iii) `test_mixed_extraction_only_persisted_categories_inserted` renamed to `test_mixed_extraction_all_three_categories_persisted`; assertion updated from `len(rows) == 2 + by_type == {used_well, upgrade_suggested}` → `len(rows) == 4 + by_type == {used_well, needs_review, upgrade_suggested}`. The `test_used_well_items_persisted` and `test_empty_extraction_inserts_nothing` tests stay byte-identical (they didn't pin Sprint 6.0's archival semantics). **(b) `backend/tests/test_vocab_skip.py`** — `_FilterRecordingBuilder` Supabase-call-chain mock gains a missing `.neq(col, val)` method that records the predicate alongside `.eq()`. Sprint 10.1.5's main-bank list endpoint added a `.neq("source_type", "needs_review")` call that the recording stub didn't know how to handle (the stub previously only supported `.eq()` + `.select()` + `.order()` + `.limit()`). Adding `.neq()` keeps the existing 10 skip-filter assertions accurate (every column predicate the route applies still gets recorded into `eq_calls`). **Backend gate: 910 passed, 15 skipped, 0 failed** in 37.59s (pre-hotfix: 906 passed, 15 skipped, 4 failed; net +4 passing tests reflect the 4 fixes). **Frontend gate: 2634/2634 pass** (unchanged from Sprint 10.1.5; this hotfix is backend-only). **Audit hotfix count 18 → 19** (Sprint 10.1.5-hotfix is a test-alignment hotfix that surfaced via CI failure — distinct from a code-bug hotfix but classified as hotfix because it fixes the CI red on PR #194). **NO production code changes.** **NO frontend changes.** **CRITICAL non-revert:** `_PERSISTED_SOURCE_TYPES = {'used_well', 'upgrade_suggested', 'needs_review'}` stays as-is — Sprint 10.1.5's whole point is to re-enable `needs_review` persistence. The bug-analysis bot's proposed revert is rejected; the correct fix is to update the stale Sprint 6.0 tests to match the new intent (the tests were pinning what Sprint 6.0 wanted, not what Sprint 10.1.5 ships). **Audit gap pre-empted for next time:** when reversing a prior sprint's deliberate filter / behaviour gate, every test that pins the previous direction must be updated in the same patch — a follow-up hotfix sprint is the recoverable path but slows the lifecycle by one CI cycle. Future sprints that reverse prior decisions should grep `tests/` for the constant name (e.g. `_PERSISTED_SOURCE_TYPES`) BEFORE pushing the implementation. **Lessons:** (a) Sprint 6.0 archival assertion lived in 3 places (constant + 2 behavioural tests) — only the constant was updated in Sprint 10.1.5, so the 2 behavioural tests broke on CI. (b) Mock stubs that pin Supabase call chains need the same maintenance as the route — when the route adds `.neq()` the stub must too. Sprint 10.1.5's frontend tests (2634 pins) caught nothing because they live in `frontend/tests/*.test.mjs` which can't exercise the Python pytest path; the backend pytest suite is the only place these contracts live.
- Sprint 10.1.5 (this PR — pre-hotfix) — **Capture re-architecture: re-enable `needs_review` + dedicated Needs Review tab (5th mode card).** Andy's redesign reverses the Sprint 6.0 archival of `source_type='needs_review'` from the capture pipeline. Sprint 6.0's reasoning was that surfacing `needs_review` items in the main vocab bank encouraged learners to memorise wrong forms; Sprint 10.1.5's reasoning is that the items ARE useful as a "learning from mistakes" surface — just not in the same bucket as items the learner used correctly. The solution: re-enable persistence, default-exclude from the main bank list endpoint, surface on a dedicated Needs Review tab in vocabulary.html as a 4th vocab-module sibling alongside my-vocab / flashcards / exercises. **Phase B Andy decisions (4, all "go with recommendations"):** (Q1) Soft delete (`is_archived=true`) preserves restorability; (Q2) NEW 5th mode card in vocabulary.html with `alert-circle` Lucide icon; (Q3) Re-enable `needs_review` capture into the dedicated tab (NOT the main bank); (Q4) Card visual = `original_word → suggestion` arrow + context + AI feedback, Mark-fixed promotes to `source_type='manual'`, AI feedback verbatim, newest-first ordering; (Q5) Hide "Needs review" filter pill from My Vocab Bank (legacy items move to new tab automatically via the backend filter switch). **Backend changes:** (a) `routers/grading.py:_PERSISTED_SOURCE_TYPES` — `needs_review` re-added to the frozenset alongside `used_well` + `upgrade_suggested` (Sprint 6.0 archival reversed; multi-line comment block updated to document the reasoning AND the new routing — main bank vs Needs Review tab); (b) `routers/vocabulary_bank.py` `GET /` list endpoint — default-excludes `source_type='needs_review'` via a `.neq("source_type", "needs_review")` filter when the caller does NOT pass an explicit `?source_type=` query param (admins / tests can still inspect needs_review rows via `?source_type=needs_review` — the filter is honoured if explicitly set); (c) NEW `GET /api/vocabulary/bank/needs-review` endpoint — returns alive `source_type='needs_review'` items ordered by `created_at DESC`, scoped to the user via Supabase RLS, fires a `vocab_needs_review_viewed` analytics event for observability; (d) NEW `POST /api/vocabulary/bank/{id}/restore` endpoint — flips `is_archived=true` back to `false` (idempotent: restoring an already-alive row returns `{ok:true, already_alive:true}` without DB write). The existing `DELETE /api/vocabulary/bank/{id}` continues to perform soft delete (`is_archived=true`) per the Sprint 7.x contract — no semantic change needed. The existing `POST /api/vocabulary/bank/{id}/mark-fixed` endpoint is reused as-is: it already flips `source_type='needs_review' → 'manual'` (Sprint 6.0 era kept the endpoint alive for triage of legacy items even after archival; Sprint 10.1.5 just routes new-capture items through the same flow). **Frontend changes:** (a) NEW `frontend/js/vocab-modules/needs-review.js` — 4th vocab-module sibling. Same `mount(container, opts) → { unmount }` contract as my-vocab / flashcards / exercises. Uses `.subpage-header` with `.subpage-header__back` Vocabulary back-link (Sprint 9.2 pattern). Card layout: `<span class="nr-card__original">{original_word}</span>` (strikethrough faded) → arrow-right Lucide icon → `<span class="nr-card__suggestion">{suggestion}</span>` (primary color, semibold) + `<p class="nr-card__context">"{context_sentence}"</p>` (italic, verbatim) + `<p class="nr-card__feedback">{reason}</p>` (AI's reason field verbatim) + 2 action buttons (`✓ Đã sửa, đưa lên flashcard` → `mark-fixed`, `🗑 Bỏ qua` → soft-delete). Intro banner (`.needs-review-intro`) frames the surface pedagogically so it reads as "AI-flagged learning opportunities" rather than "things you got wrong". Toast feedback on action success/failure. Embedded-vs-standalone routing via `opts.embedded`. Lucide `arrow-right` re-hydrated per card after `innerHTML` swap (Sprint 9.3 pattern). HTML template body contains 0 backticks (Sprint 9.1.1-hotfix sentinel preserved). (b) NEW `frontend/css/needs-review.css` — 130-line page-local stylesheet scoped to `.nr-*` BEM family. `.nr-card` shares `--av-surface-card` / `--av-border-subtle` / `--av-radius-lg` with the canonical primitives but is its OWN component (not a `.mode-card`) — different layout (flex-column with header-row inside) and different click semantic (action buttons inline, not click-to-navigate). Distinct hover treatment (border darken, no translateY). `.nr-card__btn--fix` uses `--av-primary` family; `.nr-card__btn--dismiss` uses neutral border. `.nr-toast` mirrors flashcards.css toast for visual consistency. - Sprint 9.2 (PR #191) — **In-page back-link in `.subpage-header` for vocab + speaking mode panels.** Andy reported that after entering a vocab sub-tab (my-vocab / flashcards / exercises) or a speaking mode (Luyện tập / Luyện từng Part / Full Test), the only way to return to the parent dashboard was to click the chrome's "Vocabulary" / "Speaking" nav link → full page reload. Symmetric to the activateTab() panel-toggle branch; (c) hashchange listener extended — if `fromHash` is in `VALID_TABS`, call `activateTab(fromHash, {updateHash:false})` as before; otherwise (empty or unknown hash), call `showDashboard()`. Both the in-page back-link and the browser Back button funnel through this same listener. **HTML — speaking.html (3 mode panels):** `#tab-practice` + `#tab-partbpart` + `#tab-fulltest` panels — pre-9.2 ad-hoc header (`<div class="mb-8"><p class="eyebrow">Speaking</p><h1 class="text-2xl font-bold mb-1">{title}</h1><p class="text-sm" style="...">{description}</p></div>`) replaced with the canonical `.subpage-header` primitive (`<header class="subpage-header mb-2"><div class="subpage-header__lhs"><button class="subpage-header__back" data-action="back-to-dashboard" aria-label="Quay về dashboard Speaking">…</button><span class="subpage-header__sep">|</span><h1 class="subpage-header__title">{title}</h1></div></header>`). - Sprint 9.1.1-hotfix (PR #190) — **RED bug fix: vocab modules crashed on mount due to backticks inside HTML template literal comments.** Andy's Vercel preview smoke on PR #189 (Sprint 9.1) surfaced 3 sub-pages failing to mount with `ReferenceError: header is not defined at my-vocab.js:53:25` (my-vocabulary.html, vocabulary.html#flashcards, vocabulary.html#exercises). Root cause: Sprint 9.1's retirement comments inside the 3 vocab modules' `const HTML = /* html */ \`...\`` template literals wrapped CSS class names in backticks (e.g. `<!-- Sprint 9.1 — \`.subpage-header\` primitive (components.css). The pre-9.1 \`.mv-header\` "context bar" ... -->`). Backticks inside a template literal terminate the literal early — JS parser interprets the first backtick (before `.subpage-header`) as the closing of the template, then `.subpage-header` parses as a property access, subsequent backticks reopen/reclose the literal, and somewhere in the broken parse the identifier `header` surfaces unqualified at runtime → `ReferenceError`. Total parity of backticks was even (4 in my-vocab.js, 4 in flashcards.js, 6 in exercises.js) so `node --check` and the existing test pins all passed syntactically — only runtime evaluation of the malformed but parser-acceptable structure raised the ReferenceError. **Atomic 3-item fix:** (1) strip backticks from 5 HTML-comment locations across the 3 modules (my-vocab.js lines 53-54: `\`.subpage-header\`` + `\`.mv-header\`` → no backticks + `chrome→content` arrow spelled out as `chrome to content`; flashcards.js lines 43-44: `\`.subpage-header\`` + `\`.fc-header\``; exercises.js lines 34-35: `\`.subpage-header\`` + `\`.ex-header\``; exercises.js line 62: `\`.mode-card\`` inside a 2nd Sprint 9.1 retirement comment about drill cards adopting the shared primitive). The comment semantics are preserved — backticks were decorative around CSS class names, single-quote-style not needed; bare `.classname` reads cleanly in plain text. (2) NEW sentinel test pin block `Sprint 9.1.1-hotfix — vocab module template literals must not contain backticks inside HTML body` in `frontend/tests/vocab-module-loader.test.mjs` — 3 tests (one per module) that extract the template literal between `const HTML = /* html */ \`` and the closing `\`;` using a non-greedy regex, then assert the captured body contains no backticks. This regression-guard catches the exact bug class via static analysis without needing a DOM/browser; AST-level linting would be heavier and project doesn't yet ship an ES lint config for this. (3) Ledger row + audit hotfix count bump 17 → 18 (Sprint 9.1.1 is a RED bug fix, mirroring the Sprint 6.15.4/5/6/7/8 hotfix accounting). **Frontend gate: 2588/2588 pass** (net +3 vs Sprint 9.1 baseline 2585 — the 3 new hotfix sentinel pins). **Verification:** programmatic backtick count inside template body for all 3 modules is now 0; `node --check` still passes (it always did — parity was even); but runtime evaluation no longer hits the ReferenceError. **Audit gap closed:** Sprint 9.1's pre-push verification ran `grep` for retired CSS class names + ran the full test suite but did NOT smoke-test the actual runtime module-mount paths on the Vercel preview. The Sprint 9.1 pre-push grep checks confirmed CSS structural cleanup but couldn't catch a backtick-in-template-literal runtime bug — that lives entirely in the JS evaluation surface, not the markup audit surface. **Possible Gate 12 candidate** (deferred decision pending Andy): "JavaScript template literal hygiene — HTML comments inside `/* html */` template literals must contain no backticks, even decorative ones around identifiers" — filed against this hotfix as origin. Sentinel pin (3 tests) is the immediate guard; gate formalization is the documentation layer that can land in a future methodology sprint. **Lesson surfaced:** when refactoring across JS template literal boundaries, the temptation to use backticks around CSS/HTML identifiers in inline comments is high (they look natural in Markdown-style prose). The cost is total parse fragility: any backtick inside the literal collapses the surrounding template. The fix is mechanical (drop the backticks) and the sentinel catches it; the deeper lesson is that comment-style decisions inside template literals need different conventions than top-of-file JSDoc — single quotes, asterisks, or just bare text are all safer. **NO scope creep:** Sprint 9.1's CSS lift / 3-page refactor / D3 deletion all preserved byte-identical; only 5 comment locations changed in JS files; no template literal restructuring; no markup changes; no test pin retargets (only added 3 new pins); backend untouched. **Andy testing pattern note:** the Vercel preview smoke caught this — emphasizes value of always smoke testing PR previews before merge, especially when refactors touch runtime-evaluated template surfaces. Recording it here as a process win for future sprints.
